# Generate unit tests - CodeRabbit

[CodeRabbit home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-dark.svg)](https://coderabbit.ai/)

Search...

⌘K

Search...

Navigation

Analyze & improve your code

Generate unit tests

On this page

*   [Usage​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/finishing-touches/unit-test-generation#usage%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Path Instructions​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/finishing-touches/unit-test-generation#path-instructions%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Supported software forges​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/finishing-touches/unit-test-generation#supported-software-forges%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Supported CI/CD systems​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/finishing-touches/unit-test-generation#supported-ci%2Fcd-systems%E2%80%8B)
    

This feature is available exclusively as part of the Pro plan and is not included in the Lite plan. Please refer to our [pricing page](https://www.coderabbit.ai/pricing)
 for more information about our plans and features.

This feature is in beta.

Unit Test Generation is part of the [finishing touches](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/future-development#finishing-touches)
.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/finishing-touches/unit-test-generation#usage%E2%80%8B)

Usage[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/finishing-touches/unit-test-generation#usage "Direct link to Usage")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![Unit Test Generation](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/images/finishing-touches/assets/images/utg.gif) Once you are done with your pull request and its reviews, you may want to perform finishing touches to your code, such as adding unit tests. You can request CodeRabbit to generate unit tests by typing `@coderabbitai generate unit tests` in a comment under that pull request or by clicking a checkbox under **Generate Unit Tests** in the CodeRabbit Walkthrough. Once sent, CodeRabbit will perform the following actions:

*   The CodeRabbit agent will examine your code for places where it needs tests
*   Unit tests will be generated for the PR, in a separate PR, in the same PR in a new commit, or in a comment to copy-paste, depending on your choice
*   If (and only if) you choose to generate the unit tests in a separate PR, CodeRabbit will examine your GitHub checks (build steps and tests and such) and adjust the PR to deal with build failures, test failures and similar.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/finishing-touches/unit-test-generation#path-instructions%E2%80%8B)

Path Instructions[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/finishing-touches/unit-test-generation#path-instructions "Direct link to Path Instructions")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You can customize the generated unit tests by providing instructions based on file paths in your `.coderabbit.yaml`. The `path` is a [minimatch](https://github.com/isaacs/minimatch)
 pattern.

Copy

    code_generation:  unit_tests:    path_instructions:      - path: "**/*.ts"        instructions: |          Use vitest for testing framework.          Generate comprehensive test cases including edge cases and error conditions.          Do not omit the imports; the test file must be valid.
    

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/finishing-touches/unit-test-generation#supported-software-forges%E2%80%8B)

Supported software forges[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/finishing-touches/unit-test-generation#supported-software-forges "Direct link to Supported software forges")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

These software forges are supported:

*   GitHub

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/finishing-touches/unit-test-generation#supported-ci%2Fcd-systems%E2%80%8B)

Supported CI/CD systems[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/finishing-touches/unit-test-generation#supported-cicd-systems "Direct link to Supported CI/CD systems")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

These CI/CD systems are supported for post-generation adjustments:

*   GitHub actions

[Edit this page](https://github.com/coderabbitai/coderabbit-docs/edit/main/docs/finishing-touches/unit-test-generation.md)
 Last updated on **Jul 31, 2025**

[Generate docstrings](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/finishing-touches/docstrings)
[Integrate issue tracking](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/issue-integrations)

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

# Quickstart - CodeRabbit

[CodeRabbit home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-dark.svg)](https://coderabbit.ai/)

Search...

⌘K

Search...

Navigation

Get started

Quickstart

On this page

*   [Before you begin​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/quickstart#before-you-begin%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Integrate CodeRabbit with your GitHub account​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/quickstart#integrate-coderabbit-with-your-github-account%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Add CodeRabbit to your repository​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/quickstart#add-coderabbit-to-your-repository%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Let CodeRabbit perform a code review​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/quickstart#let-coderabbit-perform-a-code-review%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Ask CodeRabbit for more information​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/quickstart#ask-coderabbit-for-more-information%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Clean up​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/quickstart#clean-up%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [What’s next​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/quickstart#what%E2%80%99s-next%E2%80%8B)
    

1

Integrate CodeRabbit into a GitHub-based repository that you own

2

Observe CodeRabbit perform a code review of a pull request that you initiate

3

Converse with CodeRabbit about the code review

4

Prompt CodeRabbit to generate its own improvements to the pull request

When you complete this tutorial, you’ll have seen CodeRabbit’s code-review feature in action, and glimpsed a few of its other AI-driven abilities as well. For a more general overview of CodeRabbit, see [Introduction](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/)
.

While this tutorial focuses on GitHub, CodeRabbit also works with GitLab, Azure DevOps, and Bitbucket. For more information, see [Integrate with Git platforms](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/platforms)
.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/quickstart#before-you-begin%E2%80%8B)

Before you begin[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/quickstart#before-you-begin "Direct link to Before you begin")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Create a new, private repository on GitHub. Name the new repository `coderabbit-test`, and let it have otherwise default GitHub settings.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/quickstart#integrate-coderabbit-with-your-github-account%E2%80%8B)

Integrate CodeRabbit with your GitHub account[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/quickstart#integrate-coderabbit-with-your-github-account "Direct link to Integrate CodeRabbit with your GitHub account")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To integrate CodeRabbit with your GitHub account, follow these steps:

1

Create an account

Visit [the CodeRabbit login page](https://app.coderabbit.ai/login?free-trial)
.

2

Login with your git provider

Click **Login with GitHub**.

3

Authorize

Click **Authorize coderabbitai**.

CodeRabbit takes a moment to set up the integration. After it finishes, the CodeRabbit dashboard appears.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/quickstart#add-coderabbit-to-your-repository%E2%80%8B)

Add CodeRabbit to your repository[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/quickstart#add-coderabbit-to-your-repository "Direct link to Add CodeRabbit to your repository")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To add CodeRabbit to your test repository, follow these steps:

1

Access repository settings

On the CodeRabbit dashboard, click **Add Repositories**. A GitHub repository-access dialog appears.

2

Grant repository access

Select the **Only select repositories** radio button.

3

Select your test repository

From the **Select repositories** menu, select the `coderabbit-test` repository that you created earlier in this Quickstart.

4

Install and authorize CodeRabbit

Click **Install & Authorize**.

CodeRabbit requests read and write access to your repository in order for its code review, issue management, and pull request generation features to work. CodeRabbit never stores your code. For more information, see [the CodeRabbit Trust Center](https://trust.coderabbit.ai/)
.

5

Complete signup if prompted

If a CodeRabbit **Complete your signup** dialog appears, then fill it out with the requested information before continuing.

CodeRabbit is now ready to use with your test repository. The next steps demonstrate its core code-review features.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/quickstart#let-coderabbit-perform-a-code-review%E2%80%8B)

Let CodeRabbit perform a code review[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/quickstart#let-coderabbit-perform-a-code-review "Direct link to Let CodeRabbit perform a code review")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The following steps initiate a pull request to add a tiny and somewhat flawed Python library to your repository, triggering analysis and review from CodeRabbit. Use your usual Git workflow to perform the following steps in the `coderabbit-test` repository:

1

Create a branch

Create a branch named `add-utils`.

2

Create a new file

In that new `add-utils` branch, create a new file called `simple_utils.py`, with the following content:

Copy

    # simple_utils.py - A tiny utility library
    
    def reverse_string(text):
        """Reverses the characters in a string."""
        return text[::-1]
    
    def count_words(sentence):
        return len(sentence.split())
    
    def celsius_to_fahrenheit(celsius):
        return (celsius * 9/5) + 32
    

3

Commit the file

Commit the added file to the `add-utils` branch. Use any text you want for the commit message.

4

Create a pull request

Create a pull request that proposes to merge the `add-utils` branch into the `main` branch. Use any text you want for the pull request message.

After a few moments, CodeRabbit responds to the pull request using the `@coderabbitai` GitHub account. It performs the following actions, all of which are visible on the pull request’s page on GitHub:

*   If you didn’t write a pull request summary, then CodeRabbit adds a new summary to the pull request.
*   CodeRabbit posts a comment titled **Walkthrough** containing analysis and commentary about the content of the pull request.
*   CodeRabbit attaches a detailed code review to the pull request as another comment.

Part of the review resembles the following screenshot: ![An example code review comment](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/images/getting-started/assets/images/quickstart-comment-9310a2af173d5afbd2c74a762e6bd808.png) This shows that CodeRabbit has noticed some flaws with this Python library, including a lack of docstrings and input validation. The review comment identifies these flaws, and suggests how you might improve them.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/quickstart#ask-coderabbit-for-more-information%E2%80%8B)

Ask CodeRabbit for more information[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/quickstart#ask-coderabbit-for-more-information "Direct link to Ask CodeRabbit for more information")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

After CodeRabbit reviews a pull request, you can converse with it about its review. You can also give CodeRabbit special commands to request it to perform specific functions, such as generating appropriate code changes for you.

1.  Post the following as a new GitHub comment attached to the pull request:
    
    Chat in PR
    
    Copy
    
        @coderabbitai Why do all of these functions need docstrings? Isn't it obvious enough what they do?
        
    
    After a few moments, CodeRabbit posts its reply, explaining its motivations for its recommendation. The reply might resemble the following:
    
    > You’re right that these functions are quite self-explanatory from their names alone. Docstrings aren’t strictly necessary for every function, especially in smaller projects with clear function names. While docstrings do provide benefits (IDE tooltips, documentation generation, help for future developers), they can sometimes feel redundant for very straightforward functions. It’s ultimately a matter of coding style and project requirements. If you prefer to skip docstrings for obvious utility functions in this project, that’s perfectly reasonable. Would you like me to adjust my review approach regarding documentation for this repository?
    
    In this case, CodeRabbit is offering to adjust its future behavior when reviewing changes to this repository. Instead, follow the next step to ask CodeRabbit to implement part of its suggestions.
2.  Post the following as another new comment:
    
    Copy
    
        @coderabbitai generate docstrings
        
    
    After a few moments, CodeRabbit does the following:
    *   CodeRabbit creates a new branch, based on `add-utils`.
    *   CodeRabbit commits changes to the branch that adds suggested docstrings to `add-utils`.
    *   CodeRabbit opens a new pull request between the new branch and `add-utils`.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/quickstart#clean-up%E2%80%8B)

Clean up[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/quickstart#clean-up "Direct link to Clean up")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Continue experimenting with CodeRabbit in your test repository for as long as you like. When you’re finished, you can delete the repository. You are now ready to add CodeRabbit to other repositories that you own, and let it review some real pull requests.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/quickstart#what%E2%80%99s-next%E2%80%8B)

What’s next[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/quickstart#whats-next "Direct link to What's next")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [Integrate CodeRabbit](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/platforms)
     with your repositories on GitHub, GitLab, Azure DevOps, or Bitbucket.
*   [Configure CodeRabbit](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/configure-coderabbit)
     beyond its default settings.
*   [Add custom review instructions](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/review-instructions)
    .
*   [Get support for CodeRabbit](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/support)
    .
*   [Learn more about how CodeRabbit works](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/overview/why-coderabbit)
    .

[Edit this page](https://github.com/coderabbitai/coderabbit-docs/edit/main/docs/getting-started/quickstart.md)
 Last updated on **Jul 31, 2025**

[CodeRabbit home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-dark.svg)](https://coderabbit.ai/)

Analyze & improve your code

Generate docstrings

On this page

*   [Usage​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/finishing-touches/docstrings#usage%E2%80%8B)

*   [Supported software forges​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/finishing-touches/docstrings#supported-software-forges%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Supported languages​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/finishing-touches/docstrings#supported-languages%E2%80%8B)
    

This feature is available exclusively as part of the Pro plan and is not included in the Lite plan. Please refer to our [pricing page](https://www.coderabbit.ai/pricing)
 for more information about our plans and features.

Docstrings generation is part of the [finishing touches](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/future-development#finishing-touches)
.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/finishing-touches/docstrings#usage%E2%80%8B)

Usage[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/finishing-touches/docstrings#usage "Direct link to Usage")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Once you are done with your pull request and its reviews, you may want to perform finishing touches to your code, such as adding in-code documentation. You can request CodeRabbit to generate docstrings by typing `@coderabbitai generate docstrings` in a comment under that pull request or by clicking the **Generate Docstrings** checkbox under **Finishing Touches** in the CodeRabbit Walkthrough. Once sent, CodeRabbit will perform the following actions:

*   All functions that are in the pull request’s changes will be fetched using `ast-grep`
*   Docstrings will be generated for the functions where they are missing or incomplete
*   These docstrings will be committed in a new branch in the same repository
*   CodeRabbit will open a pull request from this new branch to the existing pull request

Here’s an example of what a pull request may look like: ![Docstrings PR](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/images/finishing-touches/assets/images/docstrings-pull-request-9148dc697aa77238c93a4797a87f726a.png) CodeRabbit cannot perform further modifications to opened pull requests. From there, it’s your turn to checkout the branch and improve it to satisfaction. We believe that this workflow provides a significant headstart to documenting code. This feature has been rigorously tested and is now available for all Pro plan users. Additionally, you can provide feedback about this feature on [Discord](https://discord.com/channels/1134356397673414807/1317286905557287022)
.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/finishing-touches/docstrings#path-instructions%E2%80%8B)

Path Instructions[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/finishing-touches/docstrings#path-instructions "Direct link to Path Instructions")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You can customize the generated docstrings by providing instructions based on file paths in your `.coderabbit.yaml`. The `path` is a [minimatch](https://github.com/isaacs/minimatch)
 pattern.

Copy

    code_generation:  docstrings:    path_instructions:      - path: "**/*.ts"        instructions: |          End all docstrings with a notice that says "Auto-generated by CodeRabbit.".          Do not omit the closing tags; the docstring must be valid.
    

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/finishing-touches/docstrings#supported-software-forges%E2%80%8B)

Supported software forges[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/finishing-touches/docstrings#supported-software-forges "Direct link to Supported software forges")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

These software forges are supported:

*   Azure DevOps
*   GitHub
*   GitLab

While Bitbucket is not officially supported, docstrings can still be generated. However, they will be posted in a comment under the pull request. Full support for Bitbucket is planned.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/finishing-touches/docstrings#supported-languages%E2%80%8B)

Supported languages[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/finishing-touches/docstrings#supported-languages "Direct link to Supported languages")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

These languages are supported:

*   Bash
*   C
*   C#
*   C++
*   Elixir
*   Go
*   Java
*   JavaScript
*   Kotlin
*   Lua
*   Php
*   Python
*   React TypeScript
*   Ruby
*   Rust
*   Swift
*   TypeScript

CodeRabbit uses `ast-grep` to parse the code. If you want a new language to be supported, please look into [Add New Language to ast-grep](https://ast-grep.github.io/contributing/add-lang.html#add-new-language-to-ast-grep)
 first. [Edit this page](https://github.com/coderabbitai/coderabbit-docs/edit/main/docs/finishing-touches/docstrings.md)
 Last updated on **Jul 31, 2025**

[Code Graph Analysis](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/code-graph-analysis)
[Generate unit tests](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/finishing-touches/unit-test-generation)

Assistant

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

# Control and manage code reviews - CodeRabbit

[CodeRabbit home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-dark.svg)](https://coderabbit.ai/)

⌘K

Navigation

Review pull requests

Control and manage code reviews

On this page

*   [Control automatic code reviews​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#control-automatic-code-reviews%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Pause and resume automatic code reviews​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#pause-and-resume-automatic-code-reviews%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Disable automatic code reviews​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#disable-automatic-code-reviews%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Manually request code reviews​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#manually-request-code-reviews%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Resolve comments​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#resolve-comments%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Update information about the pull request​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#update-information-about-the-pull-request%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Update the summary text​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#update-the-summary-text%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Diagram the pull request history​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#diagram-the-pull-request-history%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Get information about CodeRabbit​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#get-information-about-coderabbit%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Display current configuration​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#display-current-configuration%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Display a quick-reference guide​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#display-a-quick-reference-guide%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [What’s next​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#what%E2%80%99s-next%E2%80%8B)
    

You can control CodeRabbit’s behavior with a specific pull request by mentioning the username of its bot, `@coderabbitai`, alongside keywords in comments or the pull request description, as specified by the next sections of this page. For a complete CodeRabbit command reference, see [Code review command reference](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/reference/review-commands)
.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#control-automatic-code-reviews%E2%80%8B)

Control automatic code reviews[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#flow "Direct link to Control automatic code reviews")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

By default, CodeRabbit automatically reviews every new pull request created in your repository. It updates its review with comments whenever the pull request has new commits pushed to it. The following sections show you how to tell CodeRabbit to modify this behavior with a specific pull request, such as pausing reviews, or resolving open comments. For more information about permanently configuring the behavior of CodeRabbit on your repository, see [Add a configuration file](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/configure-coderabbit)
.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#pause-and-resume-automatic-code-reviews%E2%80%8B)

Pause and resume automatic code reviews[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#pause-resume "Direct link to Pause and resume automatic code reviews")

You can tell CodeRabbit to pause its automatic reviews of a pull request. If you do, then you can still manually request CodeRabbit to review changes using the commands listed on [Code review command reference](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/reference/review-commands)
. To pause automated reviews of a pull request, post the following comment to the pull request:

Copy

    @coderabbitai pause
    

To resume automated reviews after pausing them, post the following comment to the pull request:

Copy

    @coderabbitai resume
    

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#disable-automatic-code-reviews%E2%80%8B)

Disable automatic code reviews[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#ignore "Direct link to Disable automatic code reviews")

To disable automatic code reviews for a pull request, add the following line anywhere in the pull request description:

Copy

    @coderabbitai ignore
    

As long as that text remains in the description, CodeRabbit will not automatically review any commits associated with that pull request. You can still [chat with CodeRabbit](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat)
 and issue other commands in the pull request comments. To enable automatic reviews on that pull request, delete “`@coderabbitai ignore`” from the pull request description. CodeRabbit commences automatic reviews starting with the next commit made to the branch under review.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#manually-request-code-reviews%E2%80%8B)

Manually request code reviews[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#request "Direct link to Manually request code reviews")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You can ask CodeRabbit to perform a code review at any time. This can be useful when you have paused automated code reviews. Manually requested reviews have two types:

*   A _full review_ disregards any comments that CodeRabbit has already made on this pull request, and generates a complete review of the entire pull request.
*   An _incremental review_ takes all comments that CodeRabbit has made since its most recent full review into consideration, and generates a review of only the new changes.

To manually request a full review, post the following comment to the pull request:

Copy

    @coderabbitai full review
    

To manually request an incremental review, post the following comment to the pull request:

Copy

    @coderabbitai review
    

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#resolve-comments%E2%80%8B)

Resolve comments[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#resolve "Direct link to Resolve comments")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To have CodeRabbit mark all of its previous comments as resolved, post the following comment to the pull request:

Copy

    @coderabbitai resolve
    

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#update-information-about-the-pull-request%E2%80%8B)

Update information about the pull request[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#update "Direct link to Update information about the pull request")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The commands in this section request CodeRabbit to generate and post updated information about the pull request itself.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#update-the-summary-text%E2%80%8B)

Update the summary text[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#summary "Direct link to Update the summary text")

To have CodeRabbit update the generated summary of the branch’s proposed changes to the pull request’s description, post the following comment:

Copy

    @coderabbitai summary
    

CodeRabbit updates the summary text to the description under the heading “Summary by CodeRabbit”.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#diagram-the-pull-request-history%E2%80%8B)

Diagram the pull request history[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#diagram "Direct link to Diagram the pull request history")

To have CodeRabbit post a comment that contains a sequence diagram which visualizes the history of the pull request under review, post the following comment:

Copy

    @coderabbitai generate sequence diagram
    

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#get-information-about-coderabbit%E2%80%8B)

Get information about CodeRabbit[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#info "Direct link to Get information about CodeRabbit")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The commands in this section request CodeRabbit to display its own configuration or documentation.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#display-current-configuration%E2%80%8B)

Display current configuration[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#config "Direct link to Display current configuration")

To have CodeRabbit post a comment listing out its current configuration with your repository, post the following comment to the pull request:

Copy

    @coderabbitai configuration
    

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#display-a-quick-reference-guide%E2%80%8B)

Display a quick-reference guide[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#help "Direct link to Display a quick-reference guide")

To have CodeRabbit post a comment to the pull request with a quick-reference guide to its own commands and other features, post the following comment to the pull request:

Copy

    @coderabbitai help
    

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#what%E2%80%99s-next%E2%80%8B)

What’s next[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands#whats-next "Direct link to What's next")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Review pull requests

Code review troubleshooting

If a CodeRabbit command doesn’t seem to work:

1.  Check that you have the necessary repository permissions.
2.  Verify the command syntax.
3.  Look for any response from CodeRabbit in the PR comments.
4.  Use `@coderabbitai help` for command guidance.

Need help? Join our community on [Discord](https://discord.gg/coderabbit)
 or [contact our support team](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/support)

# Set permissions - CodeRabbit

[CodeRabbit home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-dark.svg)](https://coderabbit.ai/)

Search...

⌘K

Search...

Navigation

Add CodeRabbit to your repository

Set permissions

1.  Navigate to your organization or repository settings in GitHub
2.  Go to the “GitHub Apps” or “Installed GitHub Apps” section
3.  Find CodeRabbit in the list of installed apps
4.  Click “Configure”
5.  Review and accept the new permissions

![Permission warning example](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/images/getting-started/assets/images/permission-warning-5ae71501a21d040a0a3142c6ae247393.png) ![Granting updated permissions](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/images/getting-started/assets/images/grant-permission-25e8329e13fbfa0b9b8a9c377533b58b.png) ![Updated permissions](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/images/getting-started/assets/images/updated-permissions-e69565bdcc98dca8616e78f5b0cfa46a.png) Common reasons for permission updates include:

*   Access to new GitHub features
*   Enhanced repository scanning capabilities
*   Additional workflow automation features
*   Improved security features

> Note: If you’re not an organization admin, you may need to request approval from your organization administrators to update the permissions.

After accepting the new permissions, CodeRabbit will have the access it needs to function properly. If you continue to experience issues, try refreshing your browser or reaching out to our support team. [Edit this page](https://github.com/coderabbitai/coderabbit-docs/edit/main/docs/getting-started/upgrading-permissions.md)
 Last updated on **Jul 31, 2025**

[Add organizations](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/adding-organizations)
[Overview](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/code-review-overview)

# Configure the VSCode extension - CodeRabbit

[CodeRabbit home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-dark.svg)](https://coderabbit.ai/)

Search...

⌘K

Search...

Navigation

IDE extensions

Configure the VSCode extension

On this page

*   [Find the settings screen​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/config-vscode#find-the-settings-screen%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Configure AI agent integration​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/config-vscode#configure-ai-agent-integration%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Configure automatic review behavior​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/config-vscode#configure-automatic-review-behavior%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Use with self-hosted CodeRabbit​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/config-vscode#use-with-self-hosted-coderabbit%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [What’s next​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/config-vscode#what%E2%80%99s-next%E2%80%8B)
    

This page is about configuring the CodeRabbit VSCode extension. For more information about the extension, see [Review local changes](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/code-editors)
.

The instructions on this page are specific to using the extension with VSCode. If you are instead using a VSCode-compatible editor such as Cursor or Windsurf, then the steps that you need to follow are similar, but might require some adaptation.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/config-vscode#find-the-settings-screen%E2%80%8B)

Find the settings screen[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/config-vscode#find "Direct link to Find the settings screen")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To navigate to the settings screen for the CodeRabbit VSCode extension, follow these steps:

1.  Open the CodeRabbit activity bar/sidebar.
2.  In the sidebar, click on gear shaped icon on top right(beside logout icon).
3.  You can also search for CodeRabbit: Settings in the command palette to open the settings.

The settings screen contains the following configuration controls.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/config-vscode#configure-ai-agent-integration%E2%80%8B)

Configure AI agent integration[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/config-vscode#agent "Direct link to Configure AI agent integration")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The **Agent Type** setting lets you choose the extension’s response to using the **Fix with AI** feature during code reviews. Your options are the following:

*   **Native**: The extension prompts the AI agent associated with your IDE to apply the suggested fix. This works only with VSCode(using Copilot) and Cursor(you have to start the task). If you have this option selected when using a different IDE, then the extension instead copies the prompt to your clipboard.
*   **Claude Code**: The extension opens the Terminal pane of your IDE and tries to use the `claude` command-line program to apply the suggested fix to your code. You need to have [Claude Code](https://www.anthropic.com/claude-code)
     installed for this option to be effective.
*   **Codex CLI**: The extension opens the Terminal pane of your IDE and tries to use the `codex` command-line program to apply the suggested fix to your code. You need to have [Codex CLI](https://github.com/openai/codex)
     installed for this option to be effective.
*   **OpenCode**: The extension opens the Terminal pane of your IDE and tries to use the `opencode` command-line program to apply the suggested fix to your code. You need to have [OpenCode](https://opencode.ai/)
     installed for this option to be effective.
*   **Cline**: The extension opens the `Cline` sidebar and runs a task to apply the suggested fix to your code. You need to have the [Cline](https://cline.bot/)
     extension installed for this option to be effective.
*   **Roo**: The extension opens the `Roo` sidebar and runs a task to apply the suggested fix to your code. You need to have the [Roo](https://github.com/RooCodeInc/Roo-Code)
     extension installed for this option to be effective.
*   **Kilo Code**: The extension opens the `Kilo Code` sidebar and runs a task to apply the suggested fix to your code. You need to have the [Kilo Code](https://kilocode.ai/)
     extension installed for this option to be effective.
*   **Augment Code**: The extension opens the `Augment Code` sidebar with the prompt to apply the suggested fix to your code, and you can start the task. You need to have the [Augment Code](https://www.augmentcode.com/)
     extension installed for this option to be effective.
*   **Clipboard**: The extension copies prompt text describing the suggested fix to your clipboard. From there, you can manually paste the prompt into the coding AI agent that you use with your IDE.

For more information about the **Fix with AI** feature, see [Request help from your AI coding agent](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode#agent)
.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/config-vscode#configure-automatic-review-behavior%E2%80%8B)

Configure automatic review behavior[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/config-vscode#auto-reviews "Direct link to Configure automatic review behavior")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The **Auto Review Mode** setting lets you control the behavior of the automatic code reviews that the extension can perform after you make commits to your local Git repository. Your options are the following:

*   **Disabled**: The extension doesn’t perform automatic code reviews.
*   **Prompt**: After every commit, the extension displays a dialog asking if you’d like it to perform a code review.
*   **Auto**: The extension always performs a review after every commit.

For more information about this feature, see [Automatically review local commits](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode#auto-reviews)
.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/config-vscode#use-with-self-hosted-coderabbit%E2%80%8B)

Use with self-hosted CodeRabbit[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/config-vscode#self-hosted-coderabbit "Direct link to Use with self-hosted CodeRabbit")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This setting is only used when you’re using a self-hosted instance of CodeRabbit. If you’re using the CodeRabbit Cloud service, you don’t need to configure this setting. You will need to login and logout of the extension after adding this value.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/config-vscode#what%E2%80%99s-next%E2%80%8B)

What’s next[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/config-vscode#whats-next "Direct link to What's next")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [Use the VSCode extension](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode)
    
*   [Uninstall the VSCode extension](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/uninstall-vscode)
    

[Edit this page](https://github.com/coderabbitai/coderabbit-docs/edit/main/docs/guides/config-vscode.md)
 Last updated on **Jul 31, 2025**

[Use with self-hosted CodeRabbit](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode-selfhosted)
[Uninstall the VSCode extension](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/uninstall-vscode)

Assistant

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

# Create issues - CodeRabbit

Create and resolve issues

Create issues

On this page

*   [Creating Issues Through Agentic Chat​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/issue-creation#creating-issues-through-agentic-chat%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Supported Platforms​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/issue-creation#supported-platforms%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [GitHub Issues​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/issue-creation#github-issues%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [GitLab Issues​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/issue-creation#gitlab-issues%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Jira​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/issue-creation#jira%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Linear​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/issue-creation#linear%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Tips for Issue Creation​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/issue-creation#tips-for-issue-creation%E2%80%8B)
    

This feature is available exclusively as part of the Pro plan and is not included in the Lite plan. Please refer to our [pricing page](https://www.coderabbit.ai/pricing)
 for more information about our plans and features.

CodeRabbit provides seamless issue creation capabilities across multiple platforms including GitHub, GitLab, Jira, and Linear. You can create issues directly from pull request discussions or through the agentic chat interface.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/issue-creation#creating-issues-through-agentic-chat%E2%80%8B)

Creating Issues Through Agentic Chat[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/issue-creation#creating-issues-through-agentic-chat "Direct link to Creating Issues Through Agentic Chat")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Using CodeRabbit’s chat functions, you can create issues naturally through conversations in comments or comment threads. Simply mention `@coderabbitai` and ask to create an issue. ![Creating issues inline](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/images/guides/assets/images/create-issue-inline-b91a86abf63c16c0b2c23e1a02503708.png) When using CodeRabbit’s [agentic chat](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat)
, CodeRabbit will help you format and create the issue with appropriate details based on your description and desired issue platform. ![Creating issues through agentic chat](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/images/guides/assets/images/create-issue-agentic-16f6b85f1b33448734443087830912fd.png)

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/issue-creation#supported-platforms%E2%80%8B)

Supported Platforms[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/issue-creation#supported-platforms "Direct link to Supported Platforms")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/issue-creation#github-issues%E2%80%8B)

GitHub Issues[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/issue-creation#github-issues "Direct link to GitHub Issues")

CodeRabbit can create GitHub issues directly in your repository. The integration works automatically without additional setup.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/issue-creation#gitlab-issues%E2%80%8B)

GitLab Issues[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/issue-creation#gitlab-issues "Direct link to GitLab Issues")

Similar to GitHub, GitLab issue creation is supported out of the box.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/issue-creation#jira%E2%80%8B)

Jira[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/issue-creation#jira "Direct link to Jira")

To create Jira issues, ensure you have [configured the Jira integration](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/issue-integrations#jira)
 first.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/issue-creation#linear%E2%80%8B)

Linear[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/issue-creation#linear "Direct link to Linear")

Make sure you have [set up the Linear integration](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/issue-integrations#linear)
 to create Linear issues.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/issue-creation#tips-for-issue-creation%E2%80%8B)

Tips for Issue Creation[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/issue-creation#tips-for-issue-creation "Direct link to Tips for Issue Creation")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   Use natural language when creating issues through agentic chat
*   Include code snippets when relevant
*   Specify assignees if known
*   Set appropriate priorities
*   Add deadlines or milestones if applicable

For more detailed information about issue tracking integrations, see our [Issue Integrations](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/issue-integrations)
 guide. [Edit this page](https://github.com/coderabbitai/coderabbit-docs/edit/main/docs/guides/issue-creation.md)
 Last updated on **Jul 31, 2025**

[Issue Chat](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/issue-chat)
[Linked Issues](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/linked-issues)

Assistant

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

[CodeRabbit home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-dark.svg)](https://coderabbit.ai/)

Request Changes Workflow

On this page

*   [Request Changes Workflow](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/changelog/request-changes-workflow#request-changes-workflow)
    

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/changelog/request-changes-workflow#request-changes-workflow)

Request Changes Workflow

Enable Request Changes review workflow for CodeRabbit reviews via .coderabbit.yaml under the field `request_changes_workflow` (default: false). When enabled, review comments are posted as request changes and CodeRabbit review will be marked approved once all the review comments are resolved.

# CodeRabbit Chat - CodeRabbit

[CodeRabbit home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-dark.svg)](https://coderabbit.ai/)

Search...

⌘K

Search...

Navigation

Review pull requests

CodeRabbit Chat

On this page

*   [Invocation​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#invocation%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Features​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#features%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Script Writing​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#script-writing%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Web Search​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#web-search%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Code Graph Analysis Integration​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#code-graph-analysis-integration%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Jira and Linear Integration​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#jira-and-linear-integration%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Learnings Integration​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#learnings-integration%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Single Step Code Generation​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#single-step-code-generation%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Configuration Changes​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#configuration-changes%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Agentic Chat (Chat with Planning)​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#agentic-chat-chat-with-planning-%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Help and Feedback​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#help-and-feedback%E2%80%8B)
    

This feature is available exclusively as part of the Pro plan and is not included in the Lite plan. Please refer to our [pricing page](https://www.coderabbit.ai/pricing)
 for more information about our plans and features.

CodeRabbit Chat is a powerful pull-request-specific assistant designed to streamline your development workflow. You can interact directly in pull request review comments and pull request comments to ask questions, have CodeRabbit rewrite code, or generate new code.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#invocation%E2%80%8B)

Invocation[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#invocation "Direct link to Invocation")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To invoke CodeRabbit Chat, simply comment on a pull request using the handle `@coderabbitai` without any explicit command (so without the [explicit CodeRabbit commands](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/commands)
) in plain natural language. The permission flow for the chat is the same as the deterministic CodeRabbit commands. Upon being invoked, CodeRabbit processes your request and responds with the necessary assistance. This assistance may entail generating scripts, updating issue tracking systems, offering detailed code suggestions, or even submitting an entire pull request (with your consent).

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#features%E2%80%8B)

Features[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#features "Direct link to Features")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#script-writing%E2%80%8B)

Script Writing[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#script-writing "Direct link to Script Writing")

CodeRabbit Chat can automatically generate scripts in various programming languages (mainly shell scripting) to answer questions about your codebase. If incorrect or non-running or non-germane shell scripts are created, CodeRabbit goes and tries again, and the whole script iteration process will be displayed to you in an Analysis Flow. All scripts are run in a secure sandboxed execution environment.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#web-search%E2%80%8B)

Web Search[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#web-search "Direct link to Web Search")

CodeRabbit Chat integrates real-time web search capabilities, enabling it to fetch up-to-date information to support its responses. The CodeRabbit Chat response will indicate this if it decides to search the web to answer your query. Set `enabled` to false within `web_search` within `knowledge_base` within the config in order to turn this off.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#code-graph-analysis-integration%E2%80%8B)

Code Graph Analysis Integration[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#code-graph-analysis-integration "Direct link to Code Graph Analysis Integration")

CodeRabbit Chat is capable of analyzing definitions of code symbols from the symbol graph it generates from your codebase. CodeRabbit can use these code definitions to enhance context when providing a chat response and review comments. CodeRabbit Chat will indicate in its response if it has found relevant symbols and snippets surrounding those symbols in your codebase. Set the environment variable `ENABLE_CODE_GRAPH` to false in self-hosted CodeRabbit instances to turn this feature off in self-hosted instances.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#jira-and-linear-integration%E2%80%8B)

Jira and Linear Integration[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#jira-and-linear-integration "Direct link to Jira and Linear Integration")

CodeRabbit Chat can deal with existing issue tracking system integrations in order to integrate with your existing issues. For details on setting up issue tracking integrations, see our [Issue Integrations](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/issue-integrations)
 guide and [Issue Creation](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/issue-creation)
 guide.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#learnings-integration%E2%80%8B)

Learnings Integration[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#learnings-integration "Direct link to Learnings Integration")

CodeRabbit Chat can insert and delete Learnings from your Learnings database. Simply ask it to do so in plain natural language.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#single-step-code-generation%E2%80%8B)

Single Step Code Generation[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#single-step-code-generation "Direct link to Single Step Code Generation")

For rapid prototyping and quick fixes, CodeRabbit Chat is capable of generating code snippets in a single step.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#configuration-changes%E2%80%8B)

Configuration Changes[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#configuration-changes "Direct link to Configuration Changes")

CodeRabbit is also capable of managing its own configuration settings upon request. This self-management allows the assistant to dynamically adapt to changing project requirements. By simplifying configuration updates, CodeRabbit helps users quickly adjust to new workflows or requirements without interrupting the development process.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#agentic-chat-chat-with-planning-%E2%80%8B)

Agentic Chat (Chat with Planning)[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#agentic-chat-chat-with-planning "Direct link to Agentic Chat (Chat with Planning)")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

When facing complex coding challenges, CodeRabbit Agentic Chat supports multi-step agentic flows that involve detailed planning and execution. Once the multi-step workflow is complete, CodeRabbit can automatically issue a pull request for the changes so you can consent to the code changes or edit them. CodeRabbit can also place changes in the existing pull request branch or create copyable snippets. Agent chat can be invoked explicitly with the `@coderabbitai plan` command. CodeRabbit cannot perform further modifications to opened pull requests. From there, it’s your turn to checkout the branch and improve it to satisfaction. We believe that this workflow provides a significant headstart to implementing code. Agentic Chat is currently only available on Github issue, pull request and pull request review comments.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#help-and-feedback%E2%80%8B)

Help and Feedback[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/agent_chat#help-and-feedback "Direct link to Help and Feedback")

Need help? Join our community on [Discord](https://discord.gg/coderabbit)
 or contact our support team. [Edit this page](https://github.com/coderabbitai/coderabbit-docs/edit/main/docs/guides/agent_chat.md)
 Last updated on **Jul 31, 2025**

[Code review troubleshooting](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/code-review-troubleshooting)
 [Code Graph Analysis](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/code-graph-analysis)

Assistant

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

# Install the VSCode extension - CodeRabbit

[CodeRabbit home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-dark.svg)](https://coderabbit.ai/)

Search...

⌘K

Search...

Navigation

IDE extensions

Install the VSCode extension

On this page

*   [Before you begin​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/install-vscode#before-you-begin%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Install the extension​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/install-vscode#install-the-extension%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Install using the marketplace website​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/install-vscode#install-using-the-marketplace-website%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [What’s next​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/install-vscode#what%E2%80%99s-next%E2%80%8B)
    

This page is about installing the CodeRabbit VSCode extension. For more information about the extension, see [Review local changes](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/code-editors)
.

The instructions on this page are specific to using the extension with VSCode. If you are instead using a VSCode-compatible editor such as Cursor or Windsurf, then the steps that you need to follow are similar, but might require some adaptation.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/install-vscode#before-you-begin%E2%80%8B)

Before you begin[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/install-vscode#before-you-begin "Direct link to Before you begin")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Before you can use the CodeRabbit VSCode extension, you need a CodeRabbit account. If you don’t already have an account, you can create one by visiting [the CodeRabbit login page](https://app.coderabbit.ai/login?free-trial)
.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/install-vscode#install-the-extension%E2%80%8B)

Install the extension[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/install-vscode#install-the-extension "Direct link to Install the extension")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To install the CodeRabbit extension, follow these steps:

1.  In the editor activity bar, click **Extensions**.
2.  In sidebar, type `coderabbit` into the **Search Extensions in Marketplace** search bar. After a moment, **CodeRabbit** appears in the sidebar as a search result.
3.  Select **CodeRabbit**. A summary of the CodeRabbit VSCode extension appears in the window’s main pane, along with installation controls.
4.  If you would like your editor to automatically check for and apply future updates to the extension, then keep the **Auto Update** checkbox selected. Otherwise, clear the checkbox.
5.  Click **Install**.
6.  A **Log in to CodeRabbit to get started** dialog appears. Click **Login**. If the dialog gets dismissed or times out first, then you can follow these alternate steps:
    1.  Click the CodeRabbit icon in the VSCode activity bar.
    2.  Click the **Use CodeRabbit for Free** button.
7.  Grant VSCode permission to open your browser, if asked.
8.  In your web browser, log into your CodeRabbit account.
9.  After signing in, the browser will redirect you back to VSCode. If the redirect does not occur, follow these steps:
    1.  Copy the code displayed in the success window.
    2.  Click **Paste code from browser**.
    3.  Paste the code into the input field that appears.

This connects your CodeRabbit account with the CodeRabbit VSCode extension.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/install-vscode#install-using-the-marketplace-website%E2%80%8B)

Install using the marketplace website[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/install-vscode#install-using-the-marketplace-website "Direct link to Install using the marketplace website")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If you are using the VSCode IDE, and not an IDE that derives from it such as Cursor or Windsurf, then you can alternatively obtain and install the CodeRabbit VSCode extension by visiting [the extension’s page on the Visual Studio Marketplace](https://coderabbit.link/vscode-docs)
. If you do install the extension this way, then you still need to connect your CodeRabbit account to the extension after installing it, as described in the previous section.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/install-vscode#what%E2%80%99s-next%E2%80%8B)

What’s next[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/install-vscode#whats-next "Direct link to What's next")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [Use the VSCode extension](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode)
    
*   [Configure the VSCode extension](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/config-vscode)
    
*   [Use with Self-hosted CodeRabbit](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode-selfhosted)
    

[Edit this page](https://github.com/coderabbitai/coderabbit-docs/edit/main/docs/guides/install-vscode.md)
 Last updated on **Jul 31, 2025**

[Review local changes](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/code-editors)
[Use the VSCode extension](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode)

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

# Overview - CodeRabbit

[CodeRabbit home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-dark.svg)](https://coderabbit.ai/)

Configure

Overview

On this page

*   [About CodeRabbit configuration​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/configuration-overview#about-coderabbit-configuration%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Configuration methods​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/configuration-overview#configuration-methods%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Organization settings​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/configuration-overview#organization-settings%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Repository settings​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/configuration-overview#repository-settings%E2%80%8B)

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/configuration-overview#about-coderabbit-configuration%E2%80%8B)

About CodeRabbit configuration[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/configuration-overview#about-coderabbit-configuration "Direct link to About CodeRabbit configuration")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

CodeRabbit has [a lot of configuration options](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/reference/configuration)
, with default settings that are designed to meet most needs. CodeRabbit is designed to work “out of the box”: if you don’t change any of the configuration settings away from the defaults, then CodeRabbit starts automatically adding code reviews to new pull requests in your repositories. However, understanding how to configure CodeRabbit lets you tune its behavior to the particulars of your team’s code. A few advantages of manually configuring CodeRabbit include the following:

*   Adjust the level of detail in CodeRabbit code reviews.
*   Customize review instructions to meet your specific coding standards.
*   Take advantage of agentic workflows that can speed up your review cycles.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/configuration-overview#configuration-methods%E2%80%8B)

Configuration methods[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/configuration-overview#methods "Direct link to Configuration methods")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You can configure CodeRabbit in several ways, from global organization settings down to configuration directives for specific repositories.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/configuration-overview#organization-settings%E2%80%8B)

Organization settings[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/configuration-overview#org "Direct link to Organization settings")

If you want to apply the same CodeRabbit configuration to all of your organization’s repositories, then you can manage organizational settings using the CodeRabbit web UI. For more information, see [Set your organization preferences](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/organization-settings)
.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/configuration-overview#repository-settings%E2%80%8B)

Repository settings[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/configuration-overview#repo "Direct link to Repository settings")

If you want to apply separate CodeRabbit configuration to your organization’s different repositories, then you can manage repository-specific CodeRabbit settings in two ways:

*   Add a `.coderabbit.yaml` file to the top level of your repository.
*   Use the CodeRabbit web interface.

For more information, see [Set your repository preferences](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/repository-settings)
. While the web interface provides and easier way to explore the available configuration options for your repository, we recommend using a `.coderabbit.yaml` file [as a best practice](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/setup-best-practices#yaml)
.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/configuration-overview#configuration-priority%E2%80%8B)

Configuration priority[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/configuration-overview#priority "Direct link to Configuration priority")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

CodeRabbit follows a specific hierarchy when determining which configuration settings to use. Understanding this priority system helps you manage your configuration effectively:

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/configuration-overview#priority-order-highest-to-lowest-%E2%80%8B)

Priority order (highest to lowest)[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/configuration-overview#priority-order-highest-to-lowest "Direct link to Priority order (highest to lowest)")

1.  **Local `.coderabbit.yaml` file of head branch**
2.  **Repository settings** (web UI)
3.  **Organization settings** (web UI)

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/configuration-overview#how-priority-works%E2%80%8B)

How priority works[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/configuration-overview#how-priority-works "Direct link to How priority works")

*   **If you have a local `.coderabbit.yaml` file in your head branch**: All repository and organization settings are ignored. Only the local YAML file configuration is used. Anything not defined in that file uses default settings.
*   **If you don’t have a local YAML file but have enabled repository settings**: Organization settings are ignored. Only repository settings are used.
*   **If you have organization settings and repository settings are disabled**: Only organization settings are used.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/configuration-overview#configuration-inheritance%E2%80%8B)

Configuration inheritance[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/configuration-overview#configuration-inheritance "Direct link to Configuration inheritance")

When a configuration source is active, it completely overrides all lower-priority sources. For example, if you set `reviews.tools.github-checks.timeout_ms` to `900000` in organization settings, but you have a local `.coderabbit.yaml` file that doesn’t define this setting, CodeRabbit will use the default value of `90000` instead of the organization setting. This means that configuration is not merged or inherited - the highest priority source takes complete control over all settings.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/configuration-overview#initial-configuration%E2%80%8B)

Initial configuration[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/configuration-overview#initial "Direct link to Initial configuration")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The [Initial configuration guide](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/initial-configuration)
 tours you through several settings that we recommend that you review after you set up CodeRabbit with your organization.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/configuration-overview#learnings%E2%80%8B)

Learnings[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/configuration-overview#learnings "Direct link to Learnings")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

As a complement to the configuration methods listed above, CodeRabbit keeps an internal database with _learnings_ that it collects about your team’s code review preferences, based on your interactions with the CodeRabbit bot over time. CodeRabbit learnings let you fine-tune the ways that CodeRabbit conducts its code reviews in ways that are highly specific to your repositories, and your team’s coding styles. For more information, see [Teach CodeRabbit your review preferences](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/learnings)
.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/configuration-overview#what%E2%80%99s-next%E2%80%8B)

What’s next[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/configuration-overview#whats-next "Direct link to What's next")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [Initial configuration guide](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/initial-configuration)

 Last updated on **Jul 31, 2025**
