Manage your account

Role based access

On this page

*   [Overview of CodeRabbit roles​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#overview-of-coderabbit-roles%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [CodeRabbit roles and Git platform roles​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#coderabbit-roles-and-git-platform-roles%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [CodeRabbit roles and developer features​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#coderabbit-roles-and-developer-features%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Default roles​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#default-roles%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [View or set roles​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#view-or-set-roles%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [View roles​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#view-roles%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Set roles​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#set-roles%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Add billing admin accounts​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#add-billing-admin-accounts%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Role permissions​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#role-permissions%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [What’s next​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#what%E2%80%99s-next%E2%80%8B)
    

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#overview-of-coderabbit-roles%E2%80%8B)

Overview of CodeRabbit roles[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#overview "Direct link to Overview of CodeRabbit roles")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Every CodeRabbit account has exactly one role for each organization that account is associated with. For example, if you belong to two GitHub-based organizations that use CodeRabbit, then you have one CodeRabbit role set for each of those two organizations. CodeRabbit roles determine your ability to read or change various billing, account management, and other administrative functions related to an organization. The roles are as follows:

*   **Admin**: allows full read/write access to all CodeRabbit administrative features.
*   **Member**: allows read-only access to a limited set of administrative settings. This role is appropriate for most developers in an organization.
*   **Billing Admin**: allows read/write access to features specific to a subscription and billing management, and limited access to other administrative features.

CodeRabbit users with the **Admin** role can modify the roles of other users in the organization. For a complete list of the administrative functions available to each role, see [Role permissions](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#permissions)
.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#coderabbit-roles-and-git-platform-roles%E2%80%8B)

CodeRabbit roles and Git platform roles[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#and-upstream "Direct link to CodeRabbit roles and Git platform roles")

Modifying an account’s CodeRabbit role doesn’t have any “upstream” effect on that account’s role or permissions in your organization’s Git platform. Similarly, changes to an account’s role on your organization’s Git platform don’t affect that account’s CodeRabbit role. For example, if you have CodeRabbit integrated with a GitHub organization, and you change an account’s CodeRabbit role from **Member** to **Admin**, then that account’s permission or ownership level with your GitHub organization doesn’t change as a result.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#coderabbit-roles-and-developer-features%E2%80%8B)

CodeRabbit roles and developer features[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#and-features "Direct link to CodeRabbit roles and developer features")

CodeRabbit roles affect only access to administrative features. Roles have no effect on using CodeRabbit developer features, such as automated code reviews. For example, if an organization has a Pro-tier CodeRabbit account, then any user account with a seat assigned to it can use Pro-tier features with the organization’s private repositories, regardless of that account’s role. For more information on seat and subscription management, see [Manage your subscription](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/subscription-management)
.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#default-roles%E2%80%8B)

Default roles[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#defaults "Direct link to Default roles")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

CodeRabbit assigns every user account in your organization a default role, using the following metrics:

*   If a user has an ownership-level role with the Git platform organization—for example, **Admin** on GitHub, or **Owner** on Bitbucket—then that user receives the default CodeRabbit role of **Admin**.
*   Otherwise, the user receives the **Member** role by default.

You can update a user’s role from its default setting by following the steps detailed in the next section. This requires that your own account has an **Admin** role with the organization. CodeRabbit applies these defaults only when initially setting up for an account within an organization. Subsequent “upstream” role changes don’t affect an account’s CodeRabbit role.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#view-or-set-roles%E2%80%8B)

View or set roles[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#how-to "Direct link to View or set roles")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You can view and set roles from the CodeRabbit dashboard, as detailed in the following sections.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#view-roles%E2%80%8B)

View roles[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#view-roles "Direct link to View roles")

To view a list of your organization’s role assignments, follow these steps:

1.  Go to the [CodeRabbit dashboard](https://app.coderabbit.ai/settings/repositories)
    .
2.  At the top of the sidebar, select the organization whose user roles you want to view.
3.  On the sidebar, click **Subscription**.

This displays a table of all of the CodeRabbit **Admin** and **Member** accounts associated with the selected organization. In this table, the **Role** column displays the CodeRabbit role for each account. To view a list of accounts with the **Billing Admin** role, click the **Billing Admins** tab located above the table of user accounts.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#set-roles%E2%80%8B)

Set roles[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#set-roles "Direct link to Set roles")

To modify users’ CodeRabbit accounts, your own account must have the **Admin** role within your organization.

To change a user account’s CodeRabbit role, follow these steps:

1.  Go to your organization’s list of user accounts, as detailed in the previous section. If you have the **Admin** role within this organization, then the **Role** column in the user accounts table contains selectable menus.
2.  Click the menu in the user’s **Role** column, and select the appropriate role from the list.

The only roles you can assign through this method are **Admin** and **Member**. You can’t grant the **Billing Admin** role to an existing user account. To add an account with the **Billing Admin** role, see the next section.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#add-billing-admin-accounts%E2%80%8B)

Add billing admin accounts[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#billing "Direct link to Add billing admin accounts")

Billing Admin users don’t require CodeRabbit seat licenses. You can add Billing Admin users regardless of how many seat licenses you have available.

To add a CodeRabbit user account with the **Billing Admin** role, follow these steps:

1.  Go to your organization’s list of user accounts, as detailed in [View roles](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#view-roles)
    .
2.  Click **Invite Billing Admin**.
3.  Enter the name and email address of the billing administrator who you want to invite to the organization.

This sends an email to the address that you specified. After the recipient completes the process of joining your organization in CodeRabbit, then their record appears in the user accounts list, under the **Billing Admins** tab.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#role-permissions%E2%80%8B)

Role permissions[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#permissions "Direct link to Role permissions")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The following table lists the CodeRabbit administrative functionality available to each of the CodeRabbit roles.

| Resource | Admin | Member | Billing Admin |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Learning Resources | Read/Write | Read-only | No access |
| Metrics/Dashboard | Read/Write | No access | No access |
| Reports | Read/Write | Read-only | No access |
| Integrations | Read/Write | Read-only | No access |
| Repository Settings | Read/Write | Read-only | No access |
| Organization Settings | Read/Write | Read-only | No access |
| User Management | Read/Write | Read-only | Read-only |
| Subscription Management | Read/Write | Read-only | Read/Write |
| Billing Management | Read/Write | No access | Read/Write |

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#what%E2%80%99s-next%E2%80%8B)

What’s next[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/roles#whats-next "Direct link to What's next")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [Manage your subscription](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/subscription-management)

 Last updated on **Jul 31, 2025**

# New Features and Improvements - CodeRabbit

[CodeRabbit home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-dark.svg)](https://coderabbit.ai/)

Navigation

New Features and Improvements

On this page

*   [New Features and Improvements](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/changelog/new-features-and-improvements#new-features-and-improvements)
    
*   [Learnings Page](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/changelog/new-features-and-improvements#learnings-page)
    
*   [Reports (Beta) Page](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/changelog/new-features-and-improvements#reports-beta-page)
    
*   [Sequence Diagrams Configuration](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/changelog/new-features-and-improvements#sequence-diagrams-configuration)
    
*   [Enhanced Tool Settings & New Analysis Tools](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/changelog/new-features-and-improvements#enhanced-tool-settings-%26-new-analysis-tools)

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/changelog/new-features-and-improvements#new-features-and-improvements)

New Features and Improvements

#### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/changelog/new-features-and-improvements#learnings-page)

Learnings Page

We’re thrilled to announce the new **Learnings** page! Users can now interact with learnings captured in PR comments, enhancing future reviews. Log into CodeRabbit and navigate to the Learnings tab, where you can filter learnings by Repository, File Path, and User. You can also edit or delete learnings that are no longer relevant to your project.

#### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/changelog/new-features-and-improvements#reports-beta-page)

Reports (Beta) Page

Introducing the beta release of **Reports**! Generate recurring summaries of team performance and latest PR reviews with features like:

*   Scheduling regular report generation
*   Specifying parameters such as repository, team, user, or label
*   Selecting report styles (Daily Stand-Up, Sprint Report, Release Notes, Custom)
*   Enabling your choice of delivery channel (Email, Slack, or Discord)

#### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/changelog/new-features-and-improvements#sequence-diagrams-configuration)

Sequence Diagrams Configuration

You can now choose whether to auto-generate sequence diagrams in the PR Walkthrough comment. Enable this via the CodeRabbit settings page or by setting reviews.sequence\_diagrams in the .coderabbit.yaml file.

#### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/changelog/new-features-and-improvements#enhanced-tool-settings-%26-new-analysis-tools)

Enhanced Tool Settings & New Analysis Tools

We’ve refined the default settings to be less noisy and more actionable. Additionally, we’ve added new static analysis and security tools:

*   **YAMLlint**: A linter for YAML files
*   **Gitleaks**: A lightweight, open-source secret scanner to prevent security breaches
*   **Checkov**: Scans infrastructure as code for misconfigurations before they become security issues

#### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/changelog/new-features-and-improvements#gitlab-integration-update)

GitLab Integration Update

The GitLab integration now offers more flexibility and security. Users can use Personal Access Tokens (PATs) from within their organization to post reviews. This enhancement ensures reviews are posted with appropriate organizational context and permissions, improving traceability and security.

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

# Use the VSCode extension - CodeRabbit

[CodeRabbit home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-dark.svg)](https://coderabbit.ai/)

Search...

⌘K

Search...

Navigation

IDE extensions

Use the VSCode extension

On this page

*   [Automatically review local commits​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode#automatically-review-local-commits%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Manually request code reviews​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode#manually-request-code-reviews%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Work with code reviews​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode#work-with-code-reviews%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Browse comments​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode#browse-comments%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Apply suggested changes​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode#apply-suggested-changes%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Request help from your AI coding agent​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode#request-help-from-your-ai-coding-agent%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Ignore or collapse comments​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode#ignore-or-collapse-comments%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Browse previous reviews​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode#browse-previous-reviews%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [What’s next​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode#what%E2%80%99s-next%E2%80%8B)
    

This page is about performing local code reviews using the CodeRabbit VSCode extension. For more information about the extension, see [Review local changes](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/code-editors)
. To learn how to install the extension, see [Install the VSCode extension](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/install-vscode)
. The CodeRabbit VSCode extension works by comparing changes in your current, checked-out Git branch against another branch in your local repository. You can use the extension to automatically perform full-branch changes after every commit, or make different kinds of comparisons by manually requesting a review.

The instructions on this page are specific to using the extension with VSCode. If you are instead using a VSCode-compatible editor such as Cursor or Windsurf, then the steps that you need to follow are similar, but might require some adaptation.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode#automatically-review-local-commits%E2%80%8B)

Automatically review local commits[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode#auto-reviews "Direct link to Automatically review local commits")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You can let CodeRabbit automatically review commits that you make to your local Git repository. These automatic reviews compare all committed changes against the branch that your working branch is based on. To perform an automatic review, follow these steps:

1.  Perform a Git commit using VSCode or terminal. After you do this, a dialog appears in your VSCode window, asking **Would you like to start a review?**
2.  Click **Yes**. The CodeRabbit sidebar appears in your VSCode window.
3.  Wait for the review to complete. This might take a few minutes. To cancel a review in progress, click **Stop the review**.

After the review completes, you can browse and respond to review comments as described in [Work with code reviews](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode#work)
. You can optionally configure the extension to either always or never perform automatic code reviews on commit, instead of displaying this yes-or-no dialog. For more information, see [Configure automatic review behavior](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/config-vscode#auto-reviews)
. For more control of code reviews performed using the CodeRabbit VSCode extension, you can manually request a review, as detailed in the following section.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode#manually-request-code-reviews%E2%80%8B)

Manually request code reviews[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode#manual-reviews "Direct link to Manually request code reviews")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To manually review changes in a local Git branch using the CodeRabbit VSCode extension, follow these steps:

1.  Click the CodeRabbit icon in the VSCode activity bar. The CodeRabbit sidebar appears.
2.  If you want to compare your code changes to a branch other than its base branch, then follow these steps:
    1.  In the sidebar, under **Branch**, click the name of the base branch. A **Select a base branch** dialog appears, listing other branches in your local Git repository.
    2.  Select the name of a base branch to compare against.
3.  Select one of the review-action options from the menu at the bottom of the CodeRabbit sidebar:
    *   To review all changes between the base branch and your current branch, including both committed and uncommitted changes, select **Review all changes**. This is the default selection.
    *   To limit the review to only changes on your branch that you have committed, select **Review committed changes**. This includes commits that you have pushed to your remote repository, if any, as well as any local commits.
    *   To limit the review to only uncommitted changes on your branch, select **Review uncommitted changes**. This includes both staged and unstaged changes.
4.  Refer to the list of **Files to review** in the sidebar. This list represents all of the files that the selected review action includes. To change this list of files, repeat the previous step to choose a different review action, or use Git features like `git stash` to selectively remove changes.
5.  To perform the review, click the button part of the menu. The CodeRabbit sidebar displays a **Review** section with the review’s progress.
6.  Wait for the review to complete. This might take a few minutes. To cancel a review in progress, click **Stop the review**.

After the review completes, you can browse and respond to review comments as described in the following section.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode#work-with-code-reviews%E2%80%8B)

Work with code reviews[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode#work "Direct link to Work with code reviews")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The CodeRabbit VSCode extension presents code reviews as a series of actionable comments, connected to specific files and lines. It gives you tools to apply its suggestions quickly, when possible.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode#browse-comments%E2%80%8B)

Browse comments[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode#browse "Direct link to Browse comments")

After the extension finishes its review, it adds any comments to the CodeRabbit sidebar under the **Files** heading in the **Reviews** section. Each item in **Files** is a comment referring to one or more lines in that file. Click the comment to see a detailed, inline comment in the editor, attached to the appropriate file and lines. You can react to these comments however you want: you can apply their advice literally, or let them guide you to find alternate solutions, or ignore them entirely. CodeRabbit comments are metadata stored with VSCode, and are not part of your files. The presence of comments doesn’t block your use of version control.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode#apply-suggested-changes%E2%80%8B)

Apply suggested changes[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode#apply "Direct link to Apply suggested changes")

Whenever possible, the CodeRabbit VSCode extension attaches discrete change suggestion to comments in the form of code diffs. For example, if it detects a typo in a new function name, the extension might attach a diff with a suggested correction. If you agree with CodeRabbit about the suggested fix and want to apply to exactly as it proposes, click the checkmark-shaped **Apply suggested change** icon in the inline comment. The extension makes the change for you in the editor.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode#request-help-from-your-ai-coding-agent%E2%80%8B)

Request help from your AI coding agent[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode#agent "Direct link to Request help from your AI coding agent")

If CodeRabbit determines that an AI coding agent could help with resolving one of its comments, then it adds a star-shaped **Fix with AI** icon to the inline display of that comment. To have the extension generate a request for an AI agent to address the comment, click this icon. Depending upon your IDE and the current extension settings, the extension performs one of the following actions:

*   If you are using VSCode with Copilot installed, then the extension can send the request directly to Copilot.
*   If you have Claude Code installed, then the extension can send the request to the `claude` command-line program.
*   As a fallback, the extension can copy the request, phrased as an AI prompt, to your clipboard. You can then manually paste this prompt into the coding AI of your IDE.

For more information about configuring this behavior, see [Configure AI agent integration](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/config-vscode#agent)
.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode#ignore-or-collapse-comments%E2%80%8B)

Ignore or collapse comments[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode#ignore "Direct link to Ignore or collapse comments")

To remove a comment from the editor, click its **Ignore** icon. To remove a comment but keep an icon in the editor noting its presence, click its **Collapse** icon. To see an ignored or collapsed comment in the editor again, click its summary in the CodeRabbit sidebar.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode#browse-previous-reviews%E2%80%8B)

Browse previous reviews[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode#previous "Direct link to Browse previous reviews")

If you have performed reviews prior to the most recent review in the current VSCode window, then you can browse the comments from these reviews under the **Previous reviews** heading in the CodeRabbit sidebar. If a past review comment no longer applies to the current state of your code, then clicking that comment won’t display a detailed comment or suggestion in the editor.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode#what%E2%80%99s-next%E2%80%8B)

What’s next[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode#whats-next "Direct link to What's next")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [Configure the VSCode extension](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/config-vscode)
    
*   [Uninstall the VSCode extension](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/uninstall-vscode)
    

[Edit this page](https://github.com/coderabbitai/coderabbit-docs/edit/main/docs/guides/use-vscode.md)
 Last updated on **Jul 31, 2025**

[Install the VSCode extension](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/install-vscode)
[Use with self-hosted CodeRabbit](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode-selfhosted)

Assistant

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

# Uninstall the VSCode extension - CodeRabbit

[CodeRabbit home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-dark.svg)](https://coderabbit.ai/)

IDE extensions

Uninstall the VSCode extension

On this page

*   [Uninstall the extension​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/uninstall-vscode#uninstall-the-extension%E2%80%8B)
    

This page is about uninstalling the CodeRabbit VSCode extension. For more information about the extension, see [Review local changes](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/code-editors)
.

The instructions on this page are specific to using the extension with VSCode. If you are instead using a VSCode-compatible editor such as Cursor or Windsurf, then the steps that you need to follow are similar, but might require some adaptation.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/uninstall-vscode#uninstall-the-extension%E2%80%8B)

Uninstall the extension[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/uninstall-vscode#uninstall-the-extension "Direct link to Uninstall the extension")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To uninstall the VSCode extension, follow these steps:

1.  In the VSCode activity bar, click the CodeRabbit icon.
2.  In the CodeRabbit sidebar, click the door-shaped **Logout** icon.
3.  In the VSCode activity bar, click the **Extensions** icon.
4.  In the Extensions sidebar, click the gear-shaped **Manage** icon next to CodeRabbit in the list of installed extensions.
5.  Select **Uninstall**.

[Edit this page](https://github.com/coderabbitai/coderabbit-docs/edit/main/docs/guides/uninstall-vscode.md)
 Last updated on **Jul 31, 2025**

[Configure the VSCode extension](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/config-vscode)

[CodeRabbit home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-dark.svg)](https://coderabbit.ai/)

Knowledge base

On this page

*   [Issue Tracking Integration​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/knowledge-base#issue-tracking-integration%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Learnings​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/knowledge-base#learnings%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Code Guidelines​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/knowledge-base#code-guidelines%E2%80%8B)
    

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/knowledge-base#issue-tracking-integration%E2%80%8B)

Issue Tracking Integration[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/knowledge-base#issue-tracking-integration "Direct link to Issue Tracking Integration")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

CodeRabbit can integrate with your issue tracking systems to provide better context during code reviews. For details on setting up issue tracking integrations, see our [Issue Integrations](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/issue-integrations)
 guide.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/knowledge-base#learnings%E2%80%8B)

Learnings[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/knowledge-base#learnings "Direct link to Learnings")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You can tell the bot to remember things about either specific lines in files, or generally about the entire repository, or even across repositories. For example, you can add a comment in a PR to chat directly with CodeRabbit. `@coderabbitai always remember to enforce camelCase`. Or you can comment directly on some lines of code in the PR. `@coderabbitai do not complain about lack of error handling here, it is handled higher up the execution stack.` For more information, see [Teach CodeRabbit your review preferences](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/learnings)
.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/knowledge-base#code-guidelines%E2%80%8B)

Code Guidelines[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/knowledge-base#code_guidelines "Direct link to Code Guidelines")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

CodeRabbit will analyse and learn from your organisation’s code guidelines, which you can set up in the knowledge base section. These guidelines will then be used to conduct thorough code reviews. The following patterns are scanned by default.

Copy

    **/.cursorrules
    .github/copilot-instructions.md
    **/CLAUDE.md**/
    .cursor/rules/***/
    .windsurfrules**/
    .clinerules/***/
    .rules/*
    

![Illustration of code guidelines configuration](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/images/integrations/assets/images/code-guidelines-11562724c62bf74072039fd1f8a9d9d0.png) [Edit this page](https://github.com/coderabbitai/coderabbit-docs/edit/main/docs/integrations/knowledge-base.md)
 Last updated on **Jul 31, 2025**

[Initial configuration guide](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/initial-configuration)
[Integrate MCP servers](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/context-enrichment/mcp-server-integrations)

Assistant

Responses are generated using AI and may contain mistakes.

# Use with self-hosted CodeRabbit - CodeRabbit

[CodeRabbit home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-dark.svg)](https://coderabbit.ai/)

Search...

⌘K

Search...

Navigation

IDE extensions

Use with self-hosted CodeRabbit

On this page

*   [Prerequisites​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode-selfhosted#prerequisites%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Connect your self-hosted instance​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode-selfhosted#connect-your-self-hosted-instance%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [What’s next​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode-selfhosted#what%E2%80%99s-next%E2%80%8B)
    

This page is about setting up the VSCode extension with self-hosted CodeRabbit. If you are instead using the managed offering, see [Install the VSCode extension](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/install-vscode)
.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode-selfhosted#prerequisites%E2%80%8B)

Prerequisites[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode-selfhosted#prerequisites "Direct link to Prerequisites")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  Your extension version should be greater than `0.12.1`.
2.  Logout of the extension if previously logged in.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode-selfhosted#connect-your-self-hosted-instance%E2%80%8B)

Connect your self-hosted instance[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode-selfhosted#connect-self-hosted-instance "Direct link to Connect your self-hosted instance")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To connect the VSCode extension to your self-hosted instance, follow these steps:

1.  Click on the “Self hosting CodeRabbit?” button, below the “Use CodeRabbit for free” button.
2.  Enter your self-hosted instance URL when prompted.
    *   Make sure the instance URL is reachable within your network and websocket connections are allowed.
3.  Select your git provider which you are using with your self-hosted CodeRabbit. (GitLab, Self-Hosted Gitlab, GitHub, GitHub Enterprise)
    *   If using GitHub or GitHub Enterprise, enter your [Github Personal Access Token](https://docs.github.com/en/authentication/keeping-your-account-and-data-secure/managing-your-personal-access-tokens)
         when prompted.

You should be connected to your self-hosted instance and ready to use the VSCode extension.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode-selfhosted#what%E2%80%99s-next%E2%80%8B)

What’s next[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode-selfhosted#whats-next "Direct link to What's next")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [Use the VSCode extension](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/use-vscode)
    
*   [Configure the VSCode extension](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/config-vscode)
    
*   [Uninstall the VSCode extension](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/uninstall-vscode)

# Setup best practices - CodeRabbit

[CodeRabbit home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-dark.svg)](https://coderabbit.ai/)

Best practices

Setup best practices

On this page

*   [Setup best practices​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/setup-best-practices#setup-best-practices%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Give CodeRabbit its own user account​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/setup-best-practices#give-coderabbit-its-own-user-account%E2%80%8B)

*   [What’s next​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/setup-best-practices#what%E2%80%99s-next%E2%80%8B)
    

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/setup-best-practices#setup-best-practices%E2%80%8B)

Setup best practices[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/setup-best-practices#setup "Direct link to Setup best practices")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This section lists our recommendations for setting up CodeRabbit with your Git platform, and integrating CodeRabbit with other tools and services.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/setup-best-practices#give-coderabbit-its-own-user-account%E2%80%8B)

Give CodeRabbit its own user account[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/setup-best-practices#user "Direct link to Give CodeRabbit its own user account")

CodeRabbit works best when it has a user account all to itself on your Git platform. Your team treats this account as a bot or service account—even on platforms that don’t have a formal concept of separate service accounts, such as Bitbucket Cloud. If you use GitHub, then CodeRabbit sets up a service account named `CodeRabbitAI` for you as soon as you connect your GitHub organization to CodeRabbit. On other platforms, such as Bitbucket Cloud or Gitlab, you must set this account up yourself. For platform-specific instructions about setting up this user, see [Integrate with Git platforms](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/platforms)
.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/setup-best-practices#let-coderabbit-read-your-issue-tracker%E2%80%8B)

Let CodeRabbit read your issue tracker[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/setup-best-practices#issues "Direct link to Let CodeRabbit read your issue tracker")

CodeRabbit can report on whether the changes proposed by a pull request successfully address specific, ticketed issues referenced by that pull request. For this to work, CodeRabbit needs read access to your team’s issue management system. If you use the built-in issue management of either GitHub or GitLab, then CodeRabbit issue integration works without any further setup. If you use issue management systems external from your Git platform, then you need to take additional steps to integrate CodeRabbit with your team’s issues. These are the external issue management systems that CodeRabbit supports:

*   Jira
*   Linear

For more information, see [Integrate issue tracking](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/issue-integrations)
.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/setup-best-practices#set-up-basic-reports-for-your-team%E2%80%8B)

Set up basic reports for your team[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/setup-best-practices#reports "Direct link to Set up basic reports for your team")

CodeRabbit has a flexible reporting feature that can help keep your whole team up-to-date about the latest changes to your repositories. We recommend setting up at least the following scheduled reports, using templates available through the CodeRabbit web interface:

*   A daily standup report, grouped by contributor.
*   Regular release notes, grouped by repository.

For more information, see [Generate reports](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/reports-overview)
.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/setup-best-practices#configuration-best-practices%E2%80%8B)

Configuration best practices[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/setup-best-practices#configuration "Direct link to Configuration best practices")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This section lists our recommendations for configuring the way that CodeRabbit works with your individual repositories.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/setup-best-practices#fine-tune-reviews-using-yaml-files%E2%80%8B)

Fine-tune reviews using YAML files[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/setup-best-practices#yaml "Direct link to Fine-tune reviews using YAML files")

CodeRabbit gives you two ways to configure how it works with your team’s repositories:

*   The **Organization Settings** and **Repositories** pages of [the CodeRabbit web interface](https://app.coderabbit.ai/login)
    
*   A [`.coderabbit.yaml` file](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/configure-coderabbit)
     in your repository

The web interface lets you set up your organization’s code review preferences rapidly, and can help you get familiar with CodeRabbit configuration options. We recommend adding a `.coderabbit.yaml` file to repositories, as well. Using this file has several advantages over using only the web interface:

*   It applies version control to your repository’s CodeRabbit settings, letting you track changes, view configuration history, and revert to previous configurations as needed.
*   During code reviews, CodeRabbit loads the file along with rest of your repository. This means that you can include setting changes as part of a pull request, and CodeRabbit both analyzes and applies these settings during its review.
*   The file makes the repository’s CodeRabbit settings transparent to all of the repository’s contributors.

Repository-level settings defined by a `.coderabbit.yaml` take precedence over the settings defined for that repository or for your organization using the CodeRabbit web interface. For more information, see [Add a configuration file](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/configure-coderabbit)
.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/setup-best-practices#speed-up-reviews-by-adding-path-filters%E2%80%8B)

Speed up reviews by adding path filters[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/setup-best-practices#filters "Direct link to Speed up reviews by adding path filters")

If your repository contains a lot of data or other content that CodeRabbit doesn’t need for code review context, then you can include _path filters_ in your repository configuration. For example, a filter of `!dist/**` tells CodeRabbit to disregard everything in your repository’s top-level `dist` directory when preparing a code review. Reducing the number of contextual files that CodeRabbit needs to read and analyze when preparing a code review can help make its code reviews faster. You can define path filters using the CodeRabbit web interface, or with [a `.coderabbit.yaml` file](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/configure-coderabbit)
.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/setup-best-practices#trust-the-defaults%E2%80%8B)

Trust the defaults[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/setup-best-practices#defaults "Direct link to Trust the defaults")

CodeRabbit gives you control over a number of its core code-review features, letting you deactivate them entirely for your repositories if needed. We have chosen the default settings to meet the needs of most organizations and situations, and recommend leaving these settings at their default values if possible:

*   **Cache**: Keep [the cache](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/reference/caching)
     enabled to let CodeRabbit temporarily remember details about your repository between reviews, which improves review speed.
*   **Tools**: By default, CodeRabbit is allowed to use all of the [open-source linters and analyzer tools](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/tools)
     that are available to it during code reviews. This helps CodeRabbit keep its reviews broad and flexible.
*   **Knowledge base**: CodeRabbit [knowledge base](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/knowledge-base)
     features, including learnings and issue tracking, can require data retention. If your organization needs to meet stricter data-retention policies, then you can opt out of using these features.

You can configure your use of the above features using the CodeRabbit web interface, or [a `.coderabbit.yaml` file](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/getting-started/configure-coderabbit)
.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/setup-best-practices#write-specific-ci%2Fcd-error-messages%E2%80%8B)

Write specific CI/CD error messages[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/setup-best-practices#pipeline "Direct link to Write specific CI/CD error messages")

CodeRabbit can analyze the logs of continuous integration (CI) or continuous deployment (CD) tools in your pipeline. CodeRabbit can provide better remediation advice about CI/CD failures during code reviews if your tools’ error messages are as specific as possible when reporting failures. For CodeRabbit to provide the best advice, configure your CI/CD failure output to include the following information:

*   File names associated with the failure.
*   Line numbers that identify where the failure occurred in those files.
*   An explanation of the failure, including relevant error codes or diffs.

[This pull request](https://github.com/ff14-advanced-market-search/temp-fe/pull/47/files)
 shows an example of expanding the context of a CI error, in this case including a diff to show why a code-formatter check failed.

* * *

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/setup-best-practices#what%E2%80%99s-next%E2%80%8B)

What’s next[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/setup-best-practices#whats-next "Direct link to What's next")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [Code review best practices](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/code-review-best-practices)
    

[Edit this page](https://github.com/coderabbitai/coderabbit-docs/edit/main/docs/guides/setup-best-practices.md)
 Last updated on **Jul 31, 2025**

[Code review best practices](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/code-review-best-practices)

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/issue-integrations#jira%E2%80%8B)

Jira[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/issue-integrations#jira "Direct link to Jira")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This feature is available exclusively as part of the Pro plan and is not included in the Lite plan. Please refer to our [pricing page](https://www.coderabbit.ai/pricing)
 for more information about our plans and features.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/issue-integrations#coderabbit-app%E2%80%8B)

CodeRabbit App[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/issue-integrations#coderabbit-app "Direct link to CodeRabbit App")

1.  Navigate to [integrations](https://app.coderabbit.ai/integrations)
     in the CodeRabbit app.
2.  Toggle the Jira switch to enable the integration.

Upon enabling the Jira integration, CodeRabbit will redirect you to the Jira login page. Enter your Jira credentials to authenticate the integration.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/issue-integrations#coderabbit-configuration%E2%80%8B)

CodeRabbit Configuration[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/issue-integrations#coderabbit-configuration "Direct link to CodeRabbit Configuration")

1.  Add Jira’s Project Keys to the `knowledge_base.jira.project_keys` field in your project’s CodeRabbit configuration file at `.coderabbit.yaml`.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/issue-integrations#example-usage%E2%80%8B)

Example Usage[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/issue-integrations#example-usage "Direct link to Example Usage")

You can link an issue to your pull request, allowing CodeRabbit to assess whether your changes satisfy the issue’s requirements. To link a Jira Issue, you can add the Jira Issue into the PR description as shown below.

Copy

    // (Jira Project Key - Issue Number)Closes CR-5
    

You can also create new Jira issues directly through CodeRabbit. See our [Issue Creation guide](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/issue-creation#jira)
 for details.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/issue-integrations#linear%E2%80%8B)

Linear[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/issue-integrations#Linear "Direct link to Linear")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This feature is available exclusively as part of the Pro plan and is not included in the Lite plan. Please refer to our [pricing page](https://www.coderabbit.ai/pricing)
 for more information about our plans and features.

With CodeRabbit, you can easily link your pull requests with Linear. It makes your life simpler by automatically creating Linear issues with all the code context, keeping your issues and pull requests in sync both ways. Plus, it lets you generate issues straight from pull requests, track how you’re hitting your goals, and even turn code review feedback into actionable tasks in Linear.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/issue-integrations#coderabbit-app%E2%80%8B-2)

CodeRabbit App[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/issue-integrations#coderabbit-app-1 "Direct link to CodeRabbit App")

1.  Navigate to [integrations](https://app.coderabbit.ai/integrations)
     in the CodeRabbit app.
2.  Toggle the Linear switch to enable the integration.

Upon enabling the Linear integration, CodeRabbit will redirect you to the Linear login page. Enter your Linear credentials to authenticate the integration.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/issue-integrations#coderabbit-configuration%E2%80%8B-2)

CodeRabbit Configuration[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/issue-integrations#coderabbit-configuration-1 "Direct link to CodeRabbit Configuration")

1.  Add Linear’s Team Keys to the `knowledge_base.linear.team_keys` field in your project’s CodeRabbit configuration file at `.coderabbit.yaml`.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/issue-integrations#example-usage%E2%80%8B-2)

Example Usage[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/issue-integrations#example-usage-1 "Direct link to Example Usage")

To link a Linear Issue, you can add the Linear Issue via the team key and issue number into the PR description as shown below.

Copy

    // (Linear Team Key - Issue Number)Closes ENG-123
    

You can also create new Linear issues directly through CodeRabbit. Learn more in our [Issue Creation guide](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/issue-creation#linear)
.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/issue-integrations#github%E2%80%8B)

GitHub[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/issue-integrations#github "Direct link to GitHub")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This feature is available exclusively as part of the Pro plan and is not included in the Lite plan. Please refer to our [pricing page](https://www.coderabbit.ai/pricing)
 for more information about our plans and features.

GitHub issue integration works automatically without any additional setup required.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/issue-integrations#example-usage%E2%80%8B-3)

Example Usage[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/integrations/issue-integrations#example-usage-2 "Direct link to Example Usage")

To link a GitHub Issue, you can add the issue into the PR description as shown below.

Copy

    // (# GitHub Issue Number)Closes #123

# Schedule reports - CodeRabbit

[CodeRabbit home page![light logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-light.svg)![dark logo](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/coderabbit-logo-dark.svg)](https://coderabbit.ai/)

Generate reports

Schedule reports

On this page

*   [Setting Up a Recurring Report​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#setting-up-a-recurring-report%E2%80%8B)
    
*   [Schedule Configuration​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#schedule-configuration%E2%80%8B)

*   [What’s next​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#what%E2%80%99s-next%E2%80%8B)
    

This feature is available exclusively as part of the Pro plan and is not included in the Lite plan. Please refer to our [pricing page](https://www.coderabbit.ai/pricing)
 for more information about our plans and features.

CodeRabbit Pro offers automated recurring reports that provide insights into your GitHub organization’s activities. These reports can be customized and delivered through various channels to help teams stay informed about development progress. For a conceptual overview of reports in CodeRabbit, see [Generate reports](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/reports-overview)
.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#setting-up-a-recurring-report%E2%80%8B)

Setting Up a Recurring Report[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#setting-up-a-recurring-report "Direct link to Setting Up a Recurring Report")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  Navigate to **Recurring Reports** in the [CodeRabbit dashboard](https://app.coderabbit.ai/reports/recurring)
    
2.  Click **Create Report**
3.  Configure the following settings:

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#schedule-configuration%E2%80%8B)

Schedule Configuration[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#schedule-configuration "Direct link to Schedule Configuration")

![Schedule Configuration](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/images/guides/assets/images/report-params-f367cab2fedf802ef4ad557bf4cc3da8.png) The schedule configuration allows you to set precise timing for your reports:

#### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#frequency-options%E2%80%8B)

Frequency Options[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#frequency-options "Direct link to Frequency Options")

*   **Days of Week**
    *   Select any combination of days (Sun-Sat)
    *   Set frequency (every 1-3 weeks)
    *   Ideal for weekly team syncs or sprint reviews
*   **Days of Month**
    *   Select specific dates (1-31)
    *   Special date handling:
        *   31st: Runs on the last day of every month
        *   30th: Skips February
        *   29th: Only runs in February during leap years

#### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#time-settings%E2%80%8B)

Time Settings[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#time-settings "Direct link to Time Settings")

*   Set specific time for report generation
*   Choose from comprehensive timezone list (e.g., America/New\_York)
*   Reports run at the specified time in the selected timezone

Choose a time that works for all team members, especially for distributed teams across different time zones.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#report-parameters%E2%80%8B)

Report Parameters[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#report-parameters "Direct link to Report Parameters")

Reports can be filtered using multiple parameters, match pull requests using the **IN** option and exclude pull requests using the **NOT\_IN** option:

*   **Repositories**: Select specific repositories to monitor
*   **Labels**: Filter by GitHub labels with operators:
    *   IN: Match any selected label
    *   NOT\_IN: Exclude any pr with select label
    *   ALL: Match all selected labels
*   **Users**: Filter by specific GitHub users
*   **Teams**: Filter by organization teams
    *   Note: Team filtering is not available for GitLab repositories

Each parameter can be:

*   Added or removed as needed
*   Combined with other parameters for precise filtering
*   Modified using different operators

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#report-content%E2%80%8B)

Report Content[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#report-content "Direct link to Report Content")

Reports include comprehensive PR information:

*   PR metadata:
    *   Title and description
    *   Creation and last activity dates
    *   Status (merged, mergeable, draft)
    *   State (open, closed, merged)
*   Collaboration details:
    *   Labels and reviewers
    *   Comments and discussions
    *   Team associations
*   Repository context
*   Author information

PRs are marked as stale after 168 hours (7 days) of inactivity. This helps identify potential workflow bottlenecks.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#report-templates%E2%80%8B)

Report Templates[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#report-templates "Direct link to Report Templates")

CodeRabbit offers several built-in templates:

1.  **Daily Standup Report**: A concise summary of pull requests and activities.
2.  **Sprint Report**: A structured overview of sprint goals, completed tasks, in-progress work, and blockers.
3.  **Release Notes**: A high-level changelog with summary and significant changes.
4.  **[Custom Templates](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/custom-reports)
    **: Create your own format using prompts. Allows for endless customization such as native language reporting (Japanese, Spanish, French, etc.), custom formatting, custom titles, and more.

Example custom prompt:

Copy

    Please provide a summary of:- All pull request activities- Related issues and comments- Code review discussions- Quality gate statusDo not include:- Bot conversations- Sequence diagrams
    

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#communication-channels%E2%80%8B)

Communication Channels[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#communication-channels "Direct link to Communication Channels")

Configure where your reports will be delivered: ![Report Delivery Platforms](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/coderabbit/images/guides/assets/images/report-platforms-a696bfc2f918addcfb1d762df8a8f491.png)

#### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#email%E2%80%8B)

Email[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#email "Direct link to Email")

*   Enter individual email addresses
*   Use distribution lists for team-wide delivery

#### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#slack%2Fdiscord%E2%80%8B)

Slack/Discord[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#slackdiscord "Direct link to Slack/Discord")

1.  Connect your workspace through OAuth
2.  Select target channels
3.  CodeRabbit bot will be installed automatically
4.  If installation fails check the [slack service](https://slack-status.com/)
     or [discord status](https://discordstatus.com/)
     page for any outages.

#### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#microsoft-teams%E2%80%8B)

Microsoft Teams[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#microsoft-teams "Direct link to Microsoft Teams")

1.  Create a webhook in your Teams channel
2.  Add the webhook URL to CodeRabbit
3.  Select target channels

Create separate reports if you need to send to multiple channels with different formats. Learn more about [custom report formats](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/custom-reports)
.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#managing-reports%E2%80%8B)

Managing Reports[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#managing-reports "Direct link to Managing Reports")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#preview-reports%E2%80%8B)

Preview Reports[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#preview-reports "Direct link to Preview Reports")

Test your configuration using the **Preview Report** button to generate a sample report instantly.

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#grouping-options%E2%80%8B)

Grouping Options[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#grouping-options "Direct link to Grouping Options")

Reports can be organized hierarchically using groups and subgroups:

#### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#primary-grouping%E2%80%8B)

Primary Grouping[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#primary-grouping "Direct link to Primary Grouping")

Select from these options to organize your main report structure:

*   **None**: No grouping, flat list of items
*   **Repository**: Group by source repository
*   **Label**: Group by PR labels
*   **Team**: Group by team ownership
*   **User**: Group by PR author

#### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#subgrouping%E2%80%8B)

Subgrouping[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#subgrouping "Direct link to Subgrouping")

After selecting a primary group, you can add a secondary level of organization:

*   Choose any remaining grouping option for further categorization
*   Subgroups create a nested hierarchy within primary groups
*   Select “None” to use only primary grouping

Choose grouping options that match your team’s workflow. For example:

*   Use Repository → Team for large multi-team organizations
*   Use User → Label to track individual contributions by type
*   Use Team → Repository to monitor team activity across repos

### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#report-lifecycle-management%E2%80%8B)

Report Lifecycle Management[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#report-lifecycle-management "Direct link to Report Lifecycle Management")

Control your reports through their entire lifecycle:

#### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#editing-reports%E2%80%8B)

Editing Reports[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#editing-reports "Direct link to Editing Reports")

*   Make your desired changes to any configuration settings
*   Click the **Save** button to apply your changes
*   Changes take effect from the next scheduled run

Remember to click **Save** when you’re done making changes. Your modifications will be discarded if you navigate away without saving.

#### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#disabling-reports%E2%80%8B)

Disabling Reports[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#disabling-reports "Direct link to Disabling Reports")

*   Toggle the **Active** switch to temporarily pause a report
*   Disabled reports:
    *   Maintain their configuration
    *   Skip scheduled runs
    *   Can be re-enabled at any time
    *   Show “Disabled” status in the dashboard

#### 

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#deleting-reports%E2%80%8B)

Deleting Reports[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#deleting-reports "Direct link to Deleting Reports")

*   Click the **Delete** button (trash icon) next to the report
*   Confirm deletion in the modal
*   Note: This action is permanent and cannot be undone
*   All report history and configuration will be removed

Deleting a report will immediately stop all scheduled runs and remove access to historical reports. Consider disabling instead of deleting if you might need the report again.

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#best-practices%E2%80%8B)

Best Practices[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#best-practices "Direct link to Best Practices")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1.  **Scheduling**
    *   Align report timing with your team’s workflow
    *   Consider timezone differences for distributed teams
2.  **Content**
    *   Keep prompts focused on actionable information
    *   Use grouping to improve readability
    *   Exclude unnecessary details that may create noise
3.  **Distribution**
    *   Use channels your team actively monitors
    *   Consider creating separate reports for different audiences (e.g., management vs. development team)

[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#related-resources%E2%80%8B)

Related Resources[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#related-resources "Direct link to Related Resources")

What’s next[​](https://docs.coderabbit.ai/guides/scheduled-reports#whats-next "Direct link to What's next")

Initial configuration guide
